## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard object modeled by chemical kinetics rate laws. With only (t, A) available, the most likely structures are single-species kinetic ODEs: dA_dt as a function of A (reaction order, saturation, autocatalysis) and possibly explicit time-varying rate coefficients (changing conditions, catalyst deactivation, feeding).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption when A is in large excess or surface-limited)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, pseudo-first-order conditions)
- Second-order (self-reaction) kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular consumption with both reactants tracked as A or lumped)
- n-th order power-law kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order / complex mechanism lumping)
- Linear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady-state or equilibrium concentration c1)
- Reversible first-order with conserved total: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (A ↔ B with total c2 = A + B)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics in concentration space: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth with limitation, or product-inhibited formation)
- Product-inhibited / substrate-limited rational rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (apparent saturation in consumption due to limited active sites/transport)
- Mixed-order (sum of pathways): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel first- and second-order loss channels)
- Time-varying first-order (exponentially changing conditions): dA_dt = -(c0 * exp(c1 * t)) * A (rate coefficient ramps due to temperature program or activation/deactivation captured phenomenologically)
- Time-varying first-order (power-law drift): dA_dt = -(c0 * (t + c1)**c2) * A (aging, slow changes in environment affecting k(t))
- Catalyst deactivation-like effective rate coefficient: dA_dt = -(c0 / (t + c1)) * A (rate slows over time due to fouling/deactivation or depletion of catalyst activity)
- Periodic forcing of rate (e.g., light-driven or oscillatory feed): dA_dt = -(c0 * (c1 + sin(c2 * t))) * A (time-periodic modulation of effective kinetics)
- Implicit conservation with source term (feed/production plus decay): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (continuous input with first-order removal, typical CSTR-like lumping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Sign structure: consumption-only mechanisms typically enforce dA_dt ≤ 0 for A ≥ 0 (rate laws like -c*A**n); if data show positive regions, include source terms (c0 - c1*A) or autocatalysis.
- Reaction order identification: log(-dA_dt) vs log(A) approximately linear suggests dA_dt ≈ -c0*A**c1 (power-law order c1).
- Equilibrium/steady-state: dA_dt crossing zero at A ≈ constant indicates relaxation form -c0*(A-c1) or reversible form -c0*A + c1*(c2-A).
- Parallel pathways: curvature changes in dA_dt vs A often indicate sums of orders (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2).
- Time-dependent conditions: if dA_dt at the same A differs systematically with t, model k(t) multiplicatively (dA_dt = -k(t)*A**n) using exp(c*t), (t+c)**p, or 1/(t+c).
- Capacity/limitation effects: diminishing incremental rate at high A suggests rational saturation forms like -c0*A/(A+c1) rather than pure power laws.
- Autocatalysis/inhibition: non-monotone dependence of dA_dt on A (rate increases then decreases) suggests quadratic factorization c0*A*(c1-A) or higher-order polynomials in A.
- Conservation-driven linearity: reversible A↔B with fixed total leads to dA_dt linear in A with nonzero intercept (affine in A).
- Nonnegativity constraints: physical concentrations imply A ≥ 0; prefer rate laws that do not create finite-time blow-up for A ≥ 0 unless modeling runaway autocatalysis explicitly.
